قد توهم حل وطء المرهونة. وبقاء أثر النكاح، وهو العدة، لا يبعد أن يصير سبباً؛ لأن يشتبه عليه حل وطء المعتدة بثلاث. وفي «البحر»: «الحاصل أنه إذا ظنَّ الحلّ فلا حد باتفاق الروايتين، والخلاف فيما إذا علم الحرمة، والأصح وجوبه). (1) قوله: حل وطء المرهونة؛ ذكر في «الهداية»: إنّ المستعير للرهن كالمرتهن، يعني الذي استعار أمةً من مالكها ليرهنها لو وطئها ظانا الحلّ لا يحد. ووجهه: إنه إذا استعار شيئاً ليرهنه هكذا، فهلك عند المرتهن صار المرتهن مستوفياً دينه، ووجب مثل الدين للمعير على المستعير؛ لأنه صار قابضاً دينه بالرهن، فإذا غرم للمعير صار مالكاً له، فكان بمنزلة المرتهن. [٢] قوله: وبقاء أثر النكاح... الخ؛ وجه لسقوط الحد بوطء المعتدات المذكورة، وحاصله: إن المعتدة لما كان أثر النكاح فيها باقياً وهو العدة، وكذا أثر أمومية الولد بعد الإعتاق باق، صار ذلك منشأ لظنّ حلّ وطئها، فلا يحدّ إلا إذا علم الحرمة. [٣]قوله: بثلاث؛ قال في «البحر»: «أطلق الثلاث فشمل ما إذا أوقعها جملة أو متفرقاً، ولا اعتبار بخلافِ مَن أنكر وقوع الجملة؛ لكونه مخالفاً للقطع، كذا ذكره الشارحون. وفيه نظر، لما في «صحيح مسلم» من أن الطلاق الثلاث كان واحداً في زمن النبي وأبي بكر وصدر من خلافة عمر، حتى أمضى عمر على الناس الثلاث، وإن كان العلماء قد أجابوا وأولوه فليس الدليل على وقوع الثلاث جملة بكلمة واحدة قطعياً. عنه، فإن قيل: العلماء قد أجمعوا عليه. قلنا: قد خالف أهلُ الظاهرِ في ذلك، فينبغي أن لا يحد، وإن علم الحرمة. والدليل عليه ما ذكر في «الهداية» من «كتاب النكاح» في «فصل المحرمات»: إنّ (۱) انتهى من «البحر الرائق (٥ : ١٤). كتاب الحدود الوطء الذي يوجب الحد وفي المحل: بقيام دليل ناف للحرمة ذاتاً، فلم يحد وإن أقر بحرمتها عليه والمعتدة بطلاق على مال، والمعتدة بالإعتاق حال كونها أم ولده. ثم شرع في الضرب الثَّاني من الشبهة بقوله: (وفي المحل: بقيام" دليل ناف للحرمة ذاتاً، فلم يحد وإن أقر بحرمتِها عليه الحد لا يجب بوطء المطلقة طلاقاً بائناً واحداً أو ثلاثاً مع العلم بالحرمة، على إشارة «كتاب الصلاة»، وعلى عبارة «كتاب الحدود»: يجب؛ لأنّ الملك قد زال في حق المحل فيتحقق الزنا. انتهى. وينبغي أن تحمل إشارة كتاب الصلاة على ما إذا أوقعها بكلمة واحدة، وعبارة «كتاب الحدود» على ما إذا أوقعها متفرّقاً، كما ذكر توفيقاً بينهما». انتهى. ولتطلب زيادة التفصيل من رسالتي: القول الجازم بسقوط الحد بنكاح المحارم. [١] قوله: بطلاق على مال؛ فإن كان الطلاق بلا مال فإن كان رجعياً، فمعتدته يحل الوطء بها، وإن كان بائناً بألفاظ الكنايات فسيجيء أنه من شبهة المحلّ، وذكر في «النهر»: إنه في حكم المطلقة على مال المختلعة على مال، فلو كان خلعاً خالياً عن المالِ كان من شبهة المحل. [٢) قوله: بقيام؛ يعني يوجد هناك دليل من الأدلة الشرعية دال على حل المزنية عليه؛ ولهذا تسمى هذه الشبهة حكميّة؛ أي ثابتة بحكم الشرع، فلا يحد الزاني في صورة وجودها، وإن قال: علمتُ بالحرمة لوجودِ الشبهة مع قطع النظر عن ظنّه، بخلاف ما مرّ من شبهة الفعل، فإنّه هناك لا يوجد دليلٌ على حال الموطوءة، وإنما يشتبه عليه حلّ الوطء لوجه من الوجوه. وبالجملة: في شبهة المحلّ يوجد دليل ينفي حرمة الموطوءة على الواطئ، ويثبتُ حليتها، ولو كان ذلك الدليلُ ضعيفاً، وفي شبهةِ الفعل لا أثر لذلك، وإنما يوجد دليل يورث شبهة في حرمة الوطء، ويصير باعثاً لظنه. فوضح الفرق بينهما، واندفع ما يتوهم أن ظنّه هناك أيضاً مستند إلى دليل ينفي الحرمة ويوهم الحل، فالشبهتان متساويتان. (۱) من «البحر الرائق» (٥ : ١٤).
He may have imagined the permissibility of intercourse with a pledged slave-girl. And the remaining effect of marriage, which is the 'iddah, is not unlikely to become a cause, because he is confused about the permissibility of intercourse with a woman in 'iddah by three. And in al-Bahr: 'The conclusion is that if he thought it permissible, there is no hadd by agreement of the two narrations, and the disagreement is when he knows the prohibition, and the correct opinion is that it is obligatory.' (1) His saying: Permissibility of intercourse with a pledged slave-girl; mentioned in al-Hidayah: The borrower for pledge is like the pledgee, meaning one who borrows a slave-girl from her owner to pledge her, if he has intercourse with her thinking it permissible, he is not hadded. Its reasoning: If he borrows something to pledge it in this way, and it perishes with the pledgee, the pledgee becomes satisfied his debt, and a like amount of the debt becomes obligatory upon the borrower for the lender, because he became a possessor of his debt by the pledge, so when he pays the lender he becomes owner of it, thus he is like the pledgee. [2] His saying: And the remaining effect of marriage... etc.; the reasoning for the dropping of hadd for intercourse with the mentioned women in 'iddah, and its summary: Because the woman in 'iddah has the effect of marriage remaining in her, which is the 'iddah, and likewise the effect of being Umm al-Walad after emancipation remains, that becomes a source for thinking her intercourse permissible, so he is not hadded except if he knows the prohibition. [3] His saying: By three; he said in al-Bahr: 'He used three absolutely, so it includes whether he pronounced them at once or separately, and no consideration is given to the opposition of one who denies occurrence at once because it opposes certainty, thus the commentators mentioned it.' And there is consideration, because in Sahih Muslim that triple divorce was one in the time of the Prophet and Abu Bakr and the early part of 'Umar's caliphate, until 'Umar enforced three upon the people, even though scholars answered and interpreted it, so the evidence for the occurrence of three at once with one word is not definitive. From him, if it is said: Scholars have agreed upon it. We say: The Dhahiris have opposed that, so he should not be hadded even if he knows the prohibition. And the evidence for it is what was mentioned in al-Hidayah from the Book of Nikah, in the chapter of prohibitions: (1) End from al-Bahr al-Raiq (5:14). The Book of Hudud: Intercourse that obligates Hadd. And in the subject: Due to the existence of evidence negating prohibition essentially, so he is not hadded even if he admitted its prohibition upon him, and the woman in 'iddah due to divorce for compensation, and the woman in 'iddah due to emancipation while she is Umm al-Walad. Then he began the second type of shubha with his saying: (And in the subject: Due to the existence of evidence negating prohibition essentially, so he is not hadded even if he admitted its prohibition upon him. Hadd is not obligatory for intercourse with a woman divorced irrevocably by one or three with knowledge of the prohibition, according to the indication of the Book of Prayer, and according to the wording of the Book of Hudud: It is obligatory, because ownership has ceased regarding the subject, so zina is realized. End. And the indication of the Book of Prayer should be interpreted as when he pronounced them in one word, and the wording of the Book of Hudud as when he pronounced them separately, as mentioned as a reconciliation between them. End. And for more detail, refer to my treatise: al-Qawl al-Jazim bi-Suqut al-Hadd bi-Nikah al-Maharam. [1] His saying: By divorce for compensation; if the divorce is without compensation, then if it is revocable, his 'iddah woman, it is permissible to have intercourse with her, and if it is irrevocable with kinaya words, it will come that it is from shubhat al-mahall, and it is mentioned in al-Nahr: It is in the ruling of a woman divorced for compensation like a woman who receives khul' for compensation, so if it were khul' without compensation, it would be from shubhat al-mahall. [2] His saying: Due to existence; meaning there exists evidence from the legal evidences indicating the permissibility of the woman for him; for this reason this shubha is called legal (hukmiyya), i.e., established by legal ruling, so the fornicator is not hadded in a case where it exists, even if he said: I knew the prohibition, due to the existence of shubha regardless of his assumption, contrary to what has passed of shubhat al-fi'l, because there, there is no evidence about the condition of the woman, rather he imagines the permissibility of intercourse for some reason. In summary: In shubhat al-mahall, there exists evidence negating the prohibition of the woman upon the man and establishing her permissibility, even if that evidence is weak, and in shubhat al-fi'l, there is no trace of that, rather there exists evidence that creates doubt about the prohibition of intercourse and becomes a cause for his assumption. So the difference between them is clear, and it repels what is imagined that his assumption there is also based on evidence negating prohibition and suggesting permissibility, so the two shubhas are equal. (1) From al-Bahr al-Raiq (5:14).
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on a section from the Book of Hudud dealing with the conditions under which the hadd punishment for zina is not applied due to shubha (legal ambiguity). The author explains two categories: shubhat al-fi'l (ambiguity in the act) and shubhat al-mahall (ambiguity in the subject). The first type, shubhat al-fi'l, occurs when the person mistakenly believes the act itself is permissible due to some external factor, though the woman is actually unlawful. Examples given include: a borrower who borrows a slave-girl to pledge her and then has intercourse thinking it is permissible (because he may become owner if he pays the debt); a man who has intercourse with a woman in 'iddah thinking it permissible because the effect of marriage remains; and a man who divorces his wife by three pronouncements (whether at once or separately) and then has intercourse thinking it is permissible. Regarding triple divorce, the author notes a disagreement: according to the indication of the Book of Salah, hadd is not applied, but according to the wording of the Book of Hudud, it is applied. The reconciliation is that the former applies when the three divorces were pronounced in one word, the latter when they were pronounced separately. The second type, shubhat al-mahall, occurs when there is some legal evidence (even if weak) suggesting that the woman is permissible for the man, such as in the case of a woman divorced by khul' (divorce for compensation) or a woman in 'iddah due to emancipation who is Umm al-Walad. In these cases, the man is not hadded even if he knows the prohibition, because the shubha is based on a legal ruling (hence called shubha hukmiyya). The author emphasizes the distinction between the two: in shubhat al-mahall, the evidence directly indicates permissibility of the subject; in shubhat al-fi'l, the evidence only creates a doubt about the permissibility of the act.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Legal ambiguity or doubt that prevents application of hadd.
شبهة الفعل (shubhat al-fi'l): Ambiguity concerning the act itself, where the person mistakenly thinks the act is permissible due to some reason, though the woman is unlawful.
شبهة المحل (shubhat al-mahall): Ambiguity concerning the subject (the woman), where there exists legal evidence (even weak) that the woman is permissible for the man.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband, during which the effects of marriage remain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between shubhat al-fi'l and shubhat al-mahall?
A) Shubhat al-fi'l involves the act, shubhat al-mahall involves the person.
B) Shubhat al-fi'l has no evidence about the woman's status; shubhat al-mahall has evidence even if weak.
C) Shubhat al-fi'l applies only to pledged slave-girls; shubhat al-mahall applies to divorced women.
D) There is no difference; they are the same.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is not applied when shubha exists, but the type of shubha matters: shubhat al-mahall rests on legal evidence of permissibility, while shubhat al-fi'l rests on the actor's mistaken belief about the act.

Shubha fi al-Mahall vs Shubha fi al-Fi'l: The Hanafi Distinction
Distinguishing two types of legal doubt affecting hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubha fi al-mahall and shubha fi al-fi'l, and state the Hanafi ruling on hadd and lineage for each.

Core Idea
Shubha in the subject cancels both hadd and establishes lineage; shubha in the act only cancels hadd.

In Hanafi law, the concept of shubha (legal doubt) can avert the fixed punishment (hadd) for zina. But not all shubha is equal. The key distinction is whether the doubt pertains to the woman herself (the subject) or to the act of intercourse. This distinction determines not only the punishment but also whether a child's lineage is established. We will explore this critical difference as explained in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on al-Wiqayah.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of shubha
Identify shubha fi al-mahall (doubt regarding the permissibility of the woman) and shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt regarding the permissibility of the act). Note the key difference: in shubha mahall, there is evidence (even weak) suggesting the woman is permissible; in shubha fi'l, there is no such evidence about the woman.
The evidence in shubha mahall can be a legal disagreement among scholars or an ambiguous ownership status.
2
Determine the effect on hadd
Both types of shubha prevent the application of hadd. However, the reason differs: in shubha mahall, the woman is not conclusively forbidden; in shubha fi'l, the man's mistaken belief creates doubt that averts punishment as a mercy.
In shubha mahall, hadd is cancelled even if the man admits knowing the prohibition, because the doubt is objective.
3
Determine the effect on lineage (nasab)
Only shubha mahall establishes lineage if the man claims the child. In shubha fi'l, lineage is not established because the act is considered pure zina in reality.
Lineage is based on the possibility of legitimate paternity; in shubha mahall, such possibility exists because the woman might have been permissible.
4
Apply to examples from the text
Work through the examples: intercourse with a son's slave-girl (shubha mahall), a woman in iddah from kinayah divorces (shubha mahall), and a seller with a sold item (shubha mahall). Contrast with shubha fi'l cases like a man assuming permissibility without evidence.
The commentator also reconciles an apparent contradiction between Kitab al-Salah and Kitab al-Hudud regarding a thrice-divorced woman.

Book of Hudud. Intercourse that necessitates hadd. And concerning the subject [shubha]: due to the existence of evidence negating the prohibition in essence, so he is not punished even if he admits its prohibition upon him. And [also] the woman in iddah from a divorce for compensation, and the woman in iddah from emancipation while she is the mother of his child. Then he began the second type of shubha by saying: (And concerning the subject: due to the existence of evidence negating the prohibition in essence, so he is not punished even if he admits its prohibition upon him.) Hadd is not obligatory for intercourse with a woman divorced by one or three irrevocable divorces while knowing the prohibition, according to the indication of 'Kitab al-Salah,' and according to the wording of 'Kitab al-Hudud': it is obligatory because ownership has ceased regarding the subject, so zina is realized. End. It is appropriate to interpret the indication of Kitab al-Salah as when he pronounces it with one word, and the wording of Kitab al-Hudud as when he pronounces it separately, as mentioned for reconciliation between them. End. For more detail, refer to my treatise: 'al-Qawl al-Jazim bi Suqut al-Hadd bi Nikah al-Mahrim.' [1] His saying: 'by divorce for compensation'; if the divorce is without compensation, if it is revocable, then intercourse with her during iddah is permissible, and if it is irrevocable by kinayah words, it will come that it is from shubha of the subject. And it is mentioned in 'al-Nahr': it is in the ruling of a woman divorced for compensation, a mukhala'ah for compensation. So if it is a khul' free from compensation, it would be from shubha of the subject. [2] His saying: 'due to existence'; meaning there exists some evidence from the legal evidences indicating the permissibility of the woman for him; hence this shubha is called 'hukmiyyah' (legal), i.e., established by the law's ruling. So the fornicator is not punished in its presence, even if he says: I knew the prohibition due to the existence of shubha regardless of his assumption, contrary to what passed regarding shubha of the act, for there is no evidence there regarding the state of the woman, rather he is uncertain about the permissibility of intercourse for some reason. In summary: In shubha of the subject, there exists evidence negating the prohibition of the woman for the man and establishing her permissibility, even if that evidence is weak. In shubha of the act, there is no trace of that, rather there exists evidence generating doubt about the prohibition of intercourse and prompting his assumption. So the difference between them is clear, and the misconception that his assumption there is also based on evidence negating prohibition and suggesting permissibility—so the two shubhas are equal—is repelled. (From 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' 5:14). Regarding: intercourse with his son's slave-girl, and a woman in iddah from kinayah divorces, and the seller's [intercourse with] the sold item. [1] Regarding: intercourse with his son's slave-girl, and a woman in iddah from kinayah divorces, and the seller's [intercourse with] the sold item. The repelling point: that there the evidence does not indicate the permissibility of the subject, rather it generates doubt about the permissibility of his act, contrary to shubha of the subject. And upon this the difference between them is built: the establishment of lineage (nasab) in shubha of the subject if the fornicating man claims it—i.e., the lineage of the child from his intercourse—and its non-establishment in shubha of the act, as the author will mention later. That is because lineage is something in which caution is exercised in its establishment, as detailed earlier in its chapter. Since the subject is a place of uncertainty due to the existence of evidence negating prohibition, it is necessary that lineage be established if the man claims it, contrary to the case of shubha in the act, for the act there is pure zina because he has no right in the subject due to absence of evidence indicating its permission, and establishment of lineage is a branch of establishing ownership in the subject. Hadd is only dropped due to an incidental uncertainty that occurred for him, which is insufficient for establishing lineage. [1] His saying: 'his son's slave-girl'; likewise the son of his son even if lower, even if his son is alive; likewise the mother of his daughters even if lower. So if the author had said 'his child' instead of 'his son' it would have been better due to including the daughter as well. [2] His saying: 'and a woman in iddah from kinayah divorces' is coordinated with his saying 'his son's slave-girl'; i.e., he is not punished for intercourse with a woman divorced by kinayah words during her iddah, even if he intended three [divorces] by them, so he is not punished for intercourse with her, even if he admits its prohibition upon him, because the opposing evidence exists, even if it is not acted upon in our school. Similarly, intercourse with a mukhala'ah without compensation, whether the word khul' or other, but if khul' is with compensation, it is not of this category, rather of the category of shubha in the act, as mentioned earlier, so hadd is only negated if he assumed permissibility, as in the case of a thrice-divorced woman, because no one said that a mukhala'ah for compensation falls as a revocable divorce; rather the Companions differed on whether it is a dissolution or an irrevocable divorce, so prohibition is established in all cases. This is verified in 'al-Fath.' [3] His saying: 'and the seller' is a mixed coordination as seen earlier, for it is coordinated with 'his son's slave-girl,' and the first is object, and the latter is subject of the masdar added to 'intercourse.' (From 'Fath al-Qadir' 5:255).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah discusses the legal concept of shubha (doubt) that prevents the application of hadd punishment for zina. It distinguishes between two types: shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the subject) and shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt in the act). Shubha fi al-mahall occurs when there exists some evidence, even weak, suggesting that the woman is permissible for the man, such as when a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, or with a woman in her iddah after a divorce by kinayah, or with a purchased item before delivery. In such cases, the hadd is not imposed, and if a child is born and the man claims paternity, the child's lineage is established. The reason is that the doubt pertains to the very legality of the woman (the subject), so punishment is averted and lineage is protected. In contrast, shubha fi al-fi'l occurs when the doubt is about the act itself, such as when a man mistakenly believes intercourse is permissible due to his own assumption, but there is no evidence regarding the woman's state. In such cases, hadd is still averted (due to the doubt), but lineage is not established because the act is pure zina in reality. The text also reconciles an apparent contradiction between statements in 'Kitab al-Salah' and 'Kitab al-Hudud' regarding a woman divorced by three irrevocable pronouncements: if pronounced in one session, it is shubha mahall and no hadd; if pronounced separately, it is pure zina and hadd applies. The commentator elaborates with examples, including the case of a mukhala'ah (divorce by compensation) and emphasizes that the key is whether objective evidence (even if weak) exists to indicate permissibility of the woman, not the man's subjective belief.

Key Terms
شبهة المحل (shubha al-mahall): A legal doubt concerning the subject (the woman) herself, arising from the existence of some evidence (even weak) suggesting her permissibility for the man.
شبهة الفعل (shubha al-fi'l): A legal doubt concerning the act itself, where the man mistakenly believes intercourse is permissible, but there is no evidence regarding the woman's state.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes, such as flogging for zina.
شبهة حكمية (shubha hukmiyyah): A legal doubt established by the law's ruling (shar'), as opposed to subjective doubt. It is another term for shubha mahall because it is based on objective evidence from shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on hadd and lineage in a case of shubha fi al-fi'l?
A) Hadd is averted; lineage is established.
B) Hadd is applied; lineage is not established.
C) Hadd is averted; lineage is not established.
D) Hadd is applied; lineage is established.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between shubha mahall and shubha fi'l determines not only the application of hadd but also the establishment of lineage, based on whether the doubt is objective (concerning the woman) or subjective (concerning the act).
